<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2017 Pacific typhoon season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_typhoon_climatology" title="Pacific typhoon climatology">Pacific typhoon seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2016 Pacific typhoon season">2016</a>, <b>2017</b>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2018_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2018 Pacific typhoon season">2018</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2019 Pacific typhoon season">2019</a></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2017 Pacific typhoon season</b> is an ongoing event in the annual cycle of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> formation, in which tropical cyclones form in the western Pacific Ocean. The season runs throughout 2017, though most tropical cyclones typically <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">develop</a> between May and October. The season's first named storm, Muifa, developed on April 25. This season featured the latest occurrence of the first typhoon of the year since <a href="/wiki/1998_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1998 Pacific typhoon season">1998</a>, with Noru reaching this intensity on July 23. This season featured a high amount of activity in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, but has been unusually weak, and has become one of the least active Pacific typhoon seasons on record. The scope of this article is limited to the Pacific Ocean to the north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> between <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_east" title="100th meridian east">100°E</a> and the <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">180th meridian</a>. Within the northwestern Pacific Ocean, there are two separate agencies that assign names to tropical cyclones which can often result in a cyclone having two names. The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> <small>(JMA)</small> will name a tropical cyclone should it be judged to have 10-minute <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">sustained wind speeds</a> of at least 65 km/h (40 mph) anywhere in the basin. PAGASA assigns unofficial names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility, located between 115°E–135°E and between 5°N–25°N, regardless of whether or not a tropical cyclone has already been given a name by the JMA. Tropical depressions that are monitored by the United States' <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> <small>(JTWC)</small> are given a numerical designation with a "W" suffix.</p>
<p></p>

<p>During the year several national meteorological services and scientific agencies forecast how many tropical cyclones, tropical storms, and typhoons will form during a season and/or how many tropical cyclones will affect a particular country. These agencies include the Tropical Storm Risk <small>(TSR)</small> Consortium of <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/PAGASA" title="PAGASA">PAGASA</a> and Taiwan's <a href="/wiki/Central_Weather_Bureau" title="Central Weather Bureau">Central Weather Bureau</a>. The first forecast of the year was released by PAGASA during January 20, within its seasonal climate outlook for the period January – June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAG_1_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-PAG_1-5">[5]</a></sup> The outlook noted that one to two tropical cyclones were expected between January and March, while two to four were expected to develop or enter the Philippine Area of Responsibility between April and June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAG_1_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-PAG_1-5">[5]</a></sup> During March 23, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> predicted that the tropical cyclone season in Hong Kong would be near-normal, with four to seven tropical cyclones coming within 500 km (310 mi) of the territory compared to an average of six, which was revised to six to nine tropical cyclones in August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 5, Tropical Storm Risk (TSR) issued their first forecast for the season, anticipating an activity of slightly above normal with 27 named storms, 17 typhoons and 10 intense typhoons, including an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) of 357.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_May_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_May-1">[1]</a></sup> On June 26, Taiwan's Central Weather Bureau (CWB) predicted a normal season with 21—25 tropical storms developing over the basin, while three — five systems were expected to affect Taiwan itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CWB_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-CWB-6">[6]</a></sup> In the same day, the Thai Meteorological Department (TMD) predicted that 2 tropical cyclones would move towards the northern or northeastern parts of Thailand during August or September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> On July 6, TSR released their second forecast for the season, reducing the predicted numbers to 25 named storms, 15 typhoons and 7 intense typhoons, with an ACE Index of 250.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Jul_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Jul-3">[3]</a></sup> During the same day, the PAGASA issued their second and final outlook for the season for the period of July – December, where six to nine were expected to develop or entered their area of responsibility between July and September while three to five were forecast during October to December. During August 8, the TSR released their third and final forecast for the season, slightly raising their forecast named storms to 26, with 14 reaching typhoon intensity and 7 reaching intense typhoon intensity. ACE Indices were slightly raised to 255.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Aug_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Aug-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_33da25cc795fd7f540ce799002493282" name="timeline_33da25cc795fd7f540ce799002493282">
<area alt="Typhoon Doksuri (2017)" coords="596,9,671,30" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Doksuri_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Typhoon Doksuri (2017)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Pakhar (2017)" coords="550,102,620,123" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Pakhar (2017)"/>
<area alt="Typhoon Hato (2017)" coords="543,89,602,110" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Hato_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Typhoon Hato (2017)"/>
<area alt="Typhoon Nesat (2017)" coords="486,22,550,43" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nesat_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Typhoon Nesat (2017)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Sonca (2017)" coords="484,182,548,203" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Sonca_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Sonca (2017)"/>
<area alt="Typhoon Noru (2017)" coords="507,156,565,176" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Noru_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Typhoon Noru (2017)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Talas (2017)" coords="457,142,521,163" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Talas_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Talas (2017)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Nanmadol (2017)" coords="427,102,508,123" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Nanmadol_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Nanmadol (2017)"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/33da25cc795fd7f540ce799002493282.png" usemap="#timeline_33da25cc795fd7f540ce799002493282"/></div>
</center>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> for the 2017 Pacific typhoon season, as of 18:00 UTC September 24, is 115.7525 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[nb 1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first half of the season was relatively inactive, with only seven systems developing, of which only two intensified into tropical storms. The first system of 2017 developed on January 7, and was named Auring by PAGASA. Tropical Depression Bising developed during the first week of February, and was a factor in, and worsened the effects of, the <a href="/wiki/2017_Visayas_and_Mindanao_floods" title="2017 Visayas and Mindanao floods">2017 Visayas and Mindanao floods</a>. This was followed by Crising, the third system unofficially named by PAGASA. Heavy rains from the depression caused flooding that led to the deaths of 10 people in <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a>, Philippines. Shortly after the dissipation of Crising came the formation of the first tropical storm of the season — Muifa. The system was not strong, however, and was located away from all major land areas, so it caused no damage. No systems formed during the month of May, the first such occurrence since <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013</a>. The next cyclone, Merbok, formed during mid-June, and made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> in China. The cyclone was short-lived; however, it was relatively strong, producing winds of 100 km/h (65 mph) at its peak. Nanmadol passed over the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a> and progressed to make landfall in <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a> on Japan's island of <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> during early July. Torrential rainfall and strong winds from the cyclone itself and from the stormy weather that persisted for a number of days were responsible for moderate damage and at least 36 fatalities across mainland Japan.</p>
<p>By the middle of July, tropical activity had increased with simultaneous tropical storms developing after July 14. Severe Tropical Storm Talas formed during mid-July near the <a href="/wiki/Paracel_Islands" title="Paracel Islands">Paracel Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, and traveled generally westwards. It made landfall in Vietnam after brushing China's <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a> province and, unusually, continued to track far inland to the <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>-<a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> border before weakening to a depression. At least 14 deaths were attributed to the storm, primarily as a result of flooding.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Tropical_Depression_01W_(Auring)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_01W_.28Auring.29">Tropical Depression 01W (Auring)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 01W (Auring)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg"><img alt="Auring 2017-01-08 0525z.jpg" data-file-height="10433" data-file-width="8353" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg/150px-Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg/225px-Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg/300px-Auring_2017-01-08_0525z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Auring_2017_track.png"><img alt="Auring 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Auring_2017_track.png/150px-Auring_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Auring_2017_track.png/225px-Auring_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Auring_2017_track.png/300px-Auring_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>

<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>January 7 – January 16</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>55 km/h (35 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On January 7, both PAGASA and the JMA reported that Tropical Depression Auring developed about 400 km (250 mi) to the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao City</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> During that day, the system moved along the southern periphery of a subtropical ridge of high pressure, before the JTWC initiated advisories on the system and designated it as Tropical Depression 01W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> It later made landfall in the Philippines the next day, and was assessed to have degenerated into a remnant low by the JTWC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The JMA however tracked the system until it emerged into the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By January 15, the JTWC re-issued advisories as it was located to the east of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> However, convection dissipated due to wind shear and land interaction, the JTWC issued their final warnings on January 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Flooding in <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> killed one person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Auring1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Auring1-17">[16]</a></sup> Damages from Tropical Depression Auring were totaled at <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">Ph₱</a>7.14 million (US$140,000) from agriculture and fishing in <a href="/wiki/Negros_Occidental" title="Negros Occidental">Negros Occidental</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Auring2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Auring2-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p>On February 3, a tropical depression developed near <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The system dissipated on the 7th.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. <p>A tropical depression formed over <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> on April 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> During the next 2 days, the system moved toward the Philippines</p>
<p>As of April 17, at least ten people were reported to be killed in <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> by flooding caused by the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crising1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crising1-21">[20]</a></sup> Total damages throughout the Philippines reached <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">Ph₱</a>84.8 million (US$1.7 million), mostly from <a href="/wiki/Danao,_Cebu" title="Danao, Cebu">Danao, Cebu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crising2_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crising2-22">[21]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Muifa_(Dante)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Muifa_.28Dante.29">Tropical Storm Muifa (Dante)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Muifa (Dante)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>During April 22, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression that had developed near <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Muifa_BT_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Muifa_BT-23">[22]</a></sup> After moving westward for a couple of days, the JTWC began issuing advisories, and designated the storm 03W. By April 25, 03W organized and began consolidating further as the JMA upgraded the depression to a tropical storm, giving it the name <i>Muifa</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Muifa_BT_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Muifa_BT-23">[22]</a></sup> Muifa entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility the following day, and was named <i>Dante</i> by PAGASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The storm, however, started moving northwards and immediately tracked out of the area by April 27. Following this, both the JMA and the JTWC downgraded Muifa to a tropical depression. Muifa fully dissipated early on April 29, and the JMA issued their final advisory on the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Muifa_BT_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Muifa_BT-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Merbok">Severe Tropical Storm Merbok</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Merbok">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg"><img alt="Merbok 2017-06-12 0506Z.jpg" data-file-height="7873" data-file-width="5793" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg/150px-Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg/225px-Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg/300px-Merbok_2017-06-12_0506Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Merbok_2017_track.png"><img alt="Merbok 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Merbok_2017_track.png/150px-Merbok_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Merbok_2017_track.png/225px-Merbok_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Merbok_2017_track.png/300px-Merbok_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 10 – June 13</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On June 10, the JMA started to track a tropical depression to the west of <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok_BT_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok_BT-25">[24]</a></sup> After the system entered a region favorable for further development, the depression rapidly organized, prompting the JTWC to start issuing advisories and give it the designation of 04W. A few hours later, 04W had intensified into a tropical storm, receiving the name <i>Merbok</i> as it starts to move in a north-northwestward direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok_BT_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok_BT-25">[24]</a></sup> During June 12, Merbok reached its peak intensity with 10-minute winds of 100 km/h (65 mph) and a minimum pressure of 985 hPa, shortly before making landfall in Eastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzen" title="Shenzen">Shenzen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok_BT_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok_BT-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[25]</a></sup> On June 13, the JMA issued its final warning on Merbok, as the system dissipated over China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok_BT_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok_BT-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sustained winds of 51.3 knots (95.0 km/h; 59.0 mph) and a minimum pressure of 990.3 hPa (29.24 inHg) were recorded in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> as the eye passed nearby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[25]</a></sup> Across <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guangdong_Province" title="Guangdong Province">Guangdong Province</a>, 32 homes were destroyed, 122,000 people reported property damage, and 13,000 hectares of crops flooded. Merbok killed 5 people altogether in Mainland China, 1 from Guangdong and the other 4 were from Hunan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok2_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok2-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok3_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok3-28">[27]</a></sup> Total economic losses reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">CN¥</a>516 million (US$76.7 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok1-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merbok2_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merbok2-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Nanmadol_(Emong)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Nanmadol_.28Emong.29">Severe Tropical Storm Nanmadol (Emong)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Nanmadol (Emong)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg"><img alt="Nanmadol 2017-07-03 0512Z.jpg" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="2672" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg/150px-Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg/225px-Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg/300px-Nanmadol_2017-07-03_0512Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanmadol_2017_track.png"><img alt="Nanmadol 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1855" data-file-width="2700" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Nanmadol_2017_track.png/150px-Nanmadol_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Nanmadol_2017_track.png/225px-Nanmadol_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Nanmadol_2017_track.png/300px-Nanmadol_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 1 – July 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Nanmadol_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Nanmadol (2017)">Tropical Storm Nanmadol (2017)</a></div>
<p>On July 1, the JMA upgraded a low-pressure area it had been monitoring to a tropical depression, located south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Okinotorishima" title="Okinotorishima">Okinotorishima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup> Later that day, the JMA began issuing advisories once the depression's sustained winds were estimated at 55 km/h (35 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, the PAGASA classified the system as a tropical depression, assigning the local name <i>Emong</i>. On July 2, the JMA classified the system as a tropical storm, and assigned the official name <i>Nanmadol</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup> The JTWC followed suit and gave the internal designation of 05W. The cyclone continued to intensify, and was upgraded by the JMA to a severe tropical storm later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup> Nanmadol reached peak intensity at about 06:00 UTC on July 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup> and maintained this strength until making landfall on the western coast of <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> several hours later. The cyclone began to accelerate while following a generally eastward course across the south of Japan. After brushing the southern coast of <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the JTWC issued its final advisory during the next day. The JMA followed suit late on July 4, when it had become extratropical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup> Its remnants moved out of the basin three days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol_BT_30-5"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol_BT-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evacuation advisories were issued to at least 20,000 residents due to fears of possible flooding and landslides, especially in the prefectures of <a href="/wiki/Niigata_Prefecture" title="Niigata Prefecture">Niigata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyama_Prefecture" title="Toyama Prefecture">Toyama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagano_Prefecture" title="Nagano Prefecture">Nagano</a>, which had experienced rainfall accumulations of up to 300 mm (12 in) in the preceding hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-33">[32]</a></sup> At least three people were injured during the storm—a young boy's hand was injured when a school window broke in the city of <a href="/wiki/Kumamoto" title="Kumamoto">Kumamoto</a>, and two adults in Oita prefecture sustained minor injuries after falling due to the strong winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> As of July 13, a total of 30 people have been confirmed dead due to torrential rains which caused landslides and flooding, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanmadol1_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nanmadol1-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Talas">Severe Tropical Storm Talas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Talas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg"><img alt="Talas 2017-07-16 0612Z.jpg" data-file-height="5740" data-file-width="4305" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg/150px-Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg/225px-Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg/300px-Talas_2017-07-16_0612Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talas_2017_track.png"><img alt="Talas 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Talas_2017_track.png/150px-Talas_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Talas_2017_track.png/225px-Talas_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Talas_2017_track.png/300px-Talas_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 14 – July 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>95 km/h (60 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Talas_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Talas (2017)">Tropical Storm Talas (2017)</a></div>
<p>Early on July 14, the JMA upgraded a low-pressure area in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> to a tropical depression after the system began to organize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> Late the same day, the JMA began issuing advisories on the depression, and forecast it to develop into a tropical storm within the next 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Talas made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Vinh" title="Vinh">Vinh</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ngh%E1%BB%87_An_Province" title="Nghệ An Province">Nghệ An Province</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Vietnam" title="Central Vietnam">Central Vietnam</a> at 01:00 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indochina_Time" title="Indochina Time">ICT</a> on July 17 (18:00 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on July 16) as a severe tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> In Vietnam, the storm left 14 people dead and damaged around 2,700 houses. A coal ship with 13 crew members sank off the coast of <a href="/wiki/C%E1%BB%ADa_L%C3%B2" title="Cửa Lò">Cửa Lò</a>, leaving 3 dead and another 3 still unaccounted for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Damages reached nearly 1 trillion<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_dong" title="Vietnamese dong">₫</a> (US$43.7 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talas2_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Talas2-40">[39]</a></sup> Despite making landfall in Vietnam, Talas caused a total of CNY 10.89 million(USD 1.64 million) ecomomic losses in Hainan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<td>175 km/h (110 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  935 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Noru_(2017)" title="Typhoon Noru (2017)">Typhoon Noru (2017)</a></div>
<p>The JMA reported that a non-tropical low had transitioned into a tropical depression north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> early on July 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Fluctuations in intensity occurred until late on July 29, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explosive_intensification" title="Explosive intensification">explosive intensification</a> ensued.</p>

</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 20, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression that formed over to the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Midway_Atoll" title="Midway Atoll">Midway Atoll</a>, just to the west of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulap_BT_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kulap_BT-43">[42]</a></sup> The JTWC classified the system as subtropical, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> By July 21, the subtropical storm started to show tropical characteristics, where it prompted both agencies to start issuing advisories, receiving the designation of <i>09W</i> and the name <i>Kulap</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulap_BT_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kulap_BT-43">[42]</a></sup> During the next day, Kulap briefly reached its peak intensity with 1-minute sustained winds of 95 km/h (60 mph) after imagery depicted some convection over near its compact center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> After moving westward in a marginally favorable environment, the JMA had reported a minimum pressure of 1002 hPa with peak 10-minute winds of 75 km/h (45 mph) during the early hours of July 24. However several hours later, Kulap had entered in a very unfavorable environment such as cooler waters of 25 °C (77 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Due to strong shear and an <a href="/wiki/Fujiwhara_effect" title="Fujiwhara effect">interaction</a> with Typhoon Noru to its south, Kulap had rapidly weakened; therefore, both agencies issued their final advisory on July 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> The JMA, however, tracked Kulap's remnants until July 28 when it was absorbed by the outflow of Typhoon Noru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulap_BT_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kulap_BT-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Sonca">Tropical Storm Sonca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Sonca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg"><img alt="Sonca 2017-07-25 0630Z.jpg" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="389" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg/150px-Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg/225px-Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg/300px-Sonca_2017-07-25_0630Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sonca_2017_track.png"><img alt="Sonca 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sonca_2017_track.png/150px-Sonca_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sonca_2017_track.png/225px-Sonca_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sonca_2017_track.png/300px-Sonca_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 21 – July 29</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Sonca_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Sonca (2017)">Tropical Storm Sonca (2017)</a></div>
<p>On July 21, both the JMA and the JTWC reported that Tropical Depression 08W had developed approximately 582 km (361 mi) to the south of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca_BT_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca_BT-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> After moving westward for a couple of days, the system strengthened into a tropical storm by both agencies while nearing the island province of <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>, receiving the name <i>Sonca</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca_BT_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca_BT-49">[48]</a></sup> By July 24, Sonca reached its maximum intensity with a minimum pressure of 994 hPa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca_BT_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca_BT-49">[48]</a></sup> Early on July 25, the JTWC issued its final advisory as the system made landfall over in <a href="/wiki/Qu%E1%BA%A3ng_Tr%E1%BB%8B_Province" title="Quảng Trị Province">Quảng Trị Province</a>, Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The JMA issued its final advisory a few hours later when it had weakened into a tropical depression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca_BT_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca_BT-49">[48]</a></sup> although Sonca maintained its intensity over land until it had fully dissipated on July 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca_BT_49-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca_BT-49">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Flooding in Northern Cambodia drowned two people, blocked many roads and flooded several hundred houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Damage across <a href="/wiki/Sakon_Nakhon" title="Sakon Nakhon">Sakon Nakhon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> exceeded 100 million baht (US$3 million)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonca1_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sonca1-55">[54]</a></sup> and killed 23 people across Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Roke_(Fabian)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Roke_.28Fabian.29">Tropical Storm Roke (Fabian)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Roke (Fabian)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg"><img alt="Roke 2017-07-22 0600Z.jpg" data-file-height="2834" data-file-width="2047" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg/150px-Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg/225px-Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg/300px-Roke_2017-07-22_0600Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roke_2017_track.png"><img alt="Roke 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roke_2017_track.png/150px-Roke_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roke_2017_track.png/225px-Roke_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roke_2017_track.png/300px-Roke_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 21 – July 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The JMA noted the formation of a tropical depression southeast of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> early on July 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roke_BT_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roke_BT-57">[56]</a></sup> Assigning the numerical designation <i>10W</i>, the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical depression at about 18:00 UTC the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10W_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-10W-58">[57]</a></sup> The system traveled in a generally northwesterly direction, and passed through the <a href="/wiki/Luzon_Strait" title="Luzon Strait">Luzon Strait</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10W_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-10W-58">[57]</a></sup> Around the same time, the PAGASA began issuing advisories on the depression, and contributed the unofficial name <i>Fabian</i>. Early the next day, after the system had emerged into the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, both the JMA and the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical storm, naming it <i>Roke</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10W_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-10W-58">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roke_BT_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roke_BT-57">[56]</a></sup> Roke assumed a more westerly course, and tracked obliquely towards China's <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-59">[58]</a></sup> The JTWC downgraded the system to a tropical depression just 12 hours later, at 18:00 UTC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10W_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-10W-58">[57]</a></sup> but the JMA maintained the cyclone's category as a tropical storm. Roke made landfall just east of the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> central business district at about 01:30 UTC on July 23, and passed over <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> one to two hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-59">[58]</a></sup> Roke weakened to a depression a few hours later, though the JMA declared that it had dissipated on 18:00 UTC of the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roke_BT_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Roke_BT-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Schools, businesses and government offices were closed in Hong Kong as the Hong Kong Observatory (HKO) raised its typhoon warning signal to 8—the third highest of five levels—in preparation for Tropical Storm Roke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Ferry services in the city were suspended, and more than 50 flights were delayed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> However, winds in the city were relatively light and no significant damage was reported.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Typhoon_Nesat_(Gorio)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Nesat_.28Gorio.29">Typhoon Nesat (Gorio)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Typhoon Nesat (Gorio)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg"><img alt="Nesat 2017-07-29 0530Z.jpg" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="2100" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg/150px-Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg/225px-Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg/300px-Nesat_2017-07-29_0530Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nesat_2017_track.png"><img alt="Nesat 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nesat_2017_track.png/150px-Nesat_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nesat_2017_track.png/225px-Nesat_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nesat_2017_track.png/300px-Nesat_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 25 – July 30</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  960 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nesat_(2017)" title="Typhoon Nesat (2017)">Typhoon Nesat (2017)</a></div>
<p>The JMA upgraded a low-pressure area to a tropical depression east of the Philippines early on July 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the storm not making landfall over in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Nesat enhanced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_monsoon" title="Southwest monsoon">southwest monsoon</a> which brought torrential rainfall over most of the country. As of July 30, the NDRRMC had reported a total of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippines_peso" title="Philippines peso">Php</a> 105.02 million (US$2.08 million) worth of damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gorio1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gorio1-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Haitang_(Huaning)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Haitang_.28Huaning.29">Tropical Storm Haitang (Huaning)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Haitang (Huaning)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg"><img alt="Haitang 2017-07-31 0245Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg/150px-Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg/225px-Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg/300px-Haitang_2017-07-31_0245Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haitang_2017_track.png"><img alt="Haitang 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haitang_2017_track.png/150px-Haitang_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haitang_2017_track.png/225px-Haitang_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haitang_2017_track.png/300px-Haitang_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 27 – August 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>85 km/h (50 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A low-pressure area over the northern portion of the South China Sea was upgraded to a tropical depression by the JMA early on July 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Despite an exposed LLCC with disorganized banding, the JTWC started initiating advisories, assigning the designation of <i>12W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> During the next day, the system had strengthened into a tropical storm, with the JMA naming it as <i>Haitang</i>, after ASCAT image depicted 40 knot winds over in the southern portion of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Due to the nearby Typhoon Nesat and moderate wind shear, Haitang maintained its intensity for several hours,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> until on July 30 when the system had deepened and reached its peak intensity with 10-minute sustained winds of 85 km/h (50 mph) with a minimum pressure of 985 hPa. Around the same time, Haitang entered the Philippine area of Responsibility, receiving the name <i>Huaning</i> by PAGASA, although the system had left the area during 12:00 UTC of the same day. Three hours later, the JTWC downgraded the system to a tropical depression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> though it was re-upgraded into a tropical storm six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> By July 31, the JTWC issued their final advisory on Haitang after the system had made landfall over in the <a href="/wiki/Pingtan_County" title="Pingtan County">Pingtan County</a> in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">During 06:00 UTC of that day, the JMA issued their final advisory after Haitang weakened into a remnant low.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<td>85 km/h (50 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>During July 31, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression located about 1,106 km (687 mi) to the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> During the next day, the JTWC started issuing advisories and designated it as <i>13W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> By August 2, both agencies upgraded 13W to Tropical Storm Nalgae after imagery showed flaring convection and the storm was located in a region of low to moderate wind shear and warm SSTs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Moving in a northward direction, Nalgae slowly intensified for several days. Nalgae reached its peak intensity with 10-minute sustained winds of 85 km/h (55 mph) and a minimum barometric pressure of 988 hPa during August 5 for a brief time, as it was beginning to transition into an extratropical cyclone. The JTWC downgraded Nalgae to a tropical depression later that day and issued their final advisory after the storm was located in very unfavorable environments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The JMA followed suit early on August 6 when Nalgae fully transitioned into an extratropical cyclone, after which its remnants moved further north and were last noted during August 9.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Banyan">Typhoon Banyan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Typhoon Banyan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg"><img alt="Banyan 2017-08-15 0148Z.jpg" data-file-height="3920" data-file-width="2940" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg/150px-Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg/225px-Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg/300px-Banyan_2017-08-15_0148Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banyan_2017_track.png"><img alt="Banyan 2017 track.png" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="2700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Banyan_2017_track.png/150px-Banyan_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Banyan_2017_track.png/225px-Banyan_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Banyan_2017_track.png/300px-Banyan_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 10 – August 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  955 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">On August 11, tropical depression had formed. The system then tracked north-west. On the August 12th, the systems turned north and underwent intensification (and was named Banyan) until it reached its peak of category 2 at 140km/h (85mp/h) and a pressure of 970 hPa, the storm had not developed an eye wall fully yet. After heading north, the system was disrupted by moderate-strong wind shear caused the system to weaken back to a tropical depression, now tracking north-east. Banyan managed to strengthen again into category 2 (eye did not form here) but was again affected by wind shear and cooler waters, still tracking north-east.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Typhoon_Hato_(Isang)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Hato_.28Isang.29">Typhoon Hato (Isang)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Typhoon Hato (Isang)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg"><img alt="Hato 2017-08-23 0250Z.jpg" data-file-height="7785" data-file-width="5271" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg/150px-Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg/225px-Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg/300px-Hato_2017-08-23_0250Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hato_2017_track.png"><img alt="Hato 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Hato_2017_track.png/150px-Hato_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Hato_2017_track.png/225px-Hato_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Hato_2017_track.png/300px-Hato_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 19 – August 24</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  960 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Hato" title="Typhoon Hato">Typhoon Hato</a></div>
<p>A low-pressure area developed into a tropical depression on August 19 while located to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>It gradually intensified and reached typhoon status on the afternoon of August 22 after entering the northeastern part of the South China Sea. On August 23, 07:00 HKT, Hato was approximately 100 km southeast of Hong Kong, bringing rain to the mainland as well as <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a> to the west. At 11:00 HKT the eye was approximately 60km southwest of Hong Kong with the typhoon heading onto the mainland in a west-northwesterly direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hong Kong Observatory issued Hurricane Signal No. 10 at 09:10 HKT, the first time since <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente" title="Typhoon Vicente">2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> A total of 26 people were killed while total damages in South China amounted to CN¥12.5 billion (US$1.87 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hato1_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hato1-79">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hato2_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hato2-80">[79]</a></sup> Estimated damages in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> amounted to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_dollar" title="Hong Kong dollar">HK</a>$8 billion (US$1.02 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hato3_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hato3-81">[80]</a></sup> In Macau, losses of 11.47 billion patacas (US$1.42 billion) were incurred when high tides exacerbated flooding in most of the lower lying areas, inundating ground floor shops and businesses. There were twelve deaths as a result of the typhoon including a number of people who drowned in flooded underground car-parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hato4_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hato4-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(Jolina)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_.28Jolina.29">Severe Tropical Storm Pakhar (Jolina)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Pakhar (Jolina)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg"><img alt="Pakhar 2017-08-27 0625Z.jpg" data-file-height="3627" data-file-width="2605" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg/150px-Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg/225px-Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg/300px-Pakhar_2017-08-27_0625Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pakhar_2017_track.png"><img alt="Pakhar 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pakhar_2017_track.png/150px-Pakhar_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pakhar_2017_track.png/225px-Pakhar_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pakhar_2017_track.png/300px-Pakhar_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 24 – August 27</td>
</tr>

<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
