<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Pakhar (2017)">Tropical Storm Pakhar (2017)</a></div>
<p>On August 26, Pakhar passed over the Philippines heading westward toward mainland <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> where it gathered strength before making landfall in Tianshan on August 27.</p>
<p>Total economic losses in South China have amounted to CN¥320 million (US$49 million) while a total of eight people have been killed so far as of August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakhar1_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pakhar1-83">[82]</a></sup> Moreover, damages in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> were recorded at PhP41.27 million (US$808 thousand) and 2 billion<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_dong" title="Vietnamese dong">₫</a> (US$85,000) in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakhar3_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pakhar3-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakhar2_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pakhar2-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Sanvu">Typhoon Sanvu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Typhoon Sanvu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg"><img alt="Sanvu 2017-09-01 0105Z.jpg" data-file-height="10857" data-file-width="7373" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg/150px-Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg/225px-Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg/300px-Sanvu_2017-09-01_0105Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sanvu_2017_track.png"><img alt="Sanvu 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1870" data-file-width="2700" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sanvu_2017_track.png/150px-Sanvu_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sanvu_2017_track.png/225px-Sanvu_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sanvu_2017_track.png/300px-Sanvu_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 27 – September 3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  955 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 27, the JMA began to monitor a tropical depression that had developed about 441 km (274 mi) north-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">Saipan</a>, although the system's nature was more of a monsoon depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> The JTWC followed suit on the following day, designating the system as <i>17W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Around the same time, the system had intensified into Tropical Storm Sanvu. By August 29, Sanvu increased in size, and therefore it prompted the JMA to upgrade it to a severe tropical storm. After moving in a westward direction, Sanvu stalled and entered a region of favorable conditions. As a ragged eye developed, both agencies upgraded Sanvu to a typhoon during August 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Sanvu reached its peak intensity on September 1 as a Category 2 typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> Thereafter, the system steadily weakened as it started to move northwards with JTWC immediately downgrading the system to a tropical storm and issuing their final advisory late on September 2. The JMA still classified Sanvu as a typhoon until they issued their final advisory as the system had transitioned into an extratropical cyclone on September 3.</p>
<p>Sanvu did not caused any significant damage in the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>, though a 33-year-old woman drowned in Obyan beach from tremendous waves on August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanvu1_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sanvu1-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Mawar">Severe Tropical Storm Mawar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Mawar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg"><img alt="Mawar 2017-09-03 0540Z.jpg" data-file-height="2740" data-file-width="1995" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg/150px-Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg/225px-Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg/300px-Mawar_2017-09-03_0540Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mawar_2017_track.png"><img alt="Mawar 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mawar_2017_track.png/150px-Mawar_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mawar_2017_track.png/225px-Mawar_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mawar_2017_track.png/300px-Mawar_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 30 – September 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>95 km/h (60 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 30, the JMA started to track a tropical depression to the north-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Giving the international designation of <i>18W</i> by the JTWC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> the JMA upgraded the system immediately to Tropical Storm Mawar. Slowly organizing, convection had rapidly developed and Mawar strengthened into a severe tropical storm early on September 2. On September 3, Mawar had weakened to a tropical storm after environments started to become unfavorable due to high wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Later that day, Mawar weakened to a tropical depression and the JTWC issued their final advisory while making landfall over in Southeastern China between the cities of <a href="/wiki/Shanwei" title="Shanwei">Shanwei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">Shantou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mawar1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mawar1-94">[93]</a></sup> The JMA followed suit early on September 4 when Mawar had fully dissipated.</p>
<p>The China's National Meteorological Center (NMC) issued a blue alert for the southern parts of <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Guandong" title="Guandong">Guandong</a> on September 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> During 2:00 a.m. local time on September 2, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> issued a Tropical Cyclone Warning Signal No. 1 over in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Chinese authorities activated a natural disaster alert and response to help local civil affairs departments in areas such as the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> and Guandong to prepare for relief work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> By September 3, the NMC had raised their warning signal to a yellow alert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Mawar did not cause any casualties or any major damages, though flooding was a major concern with reports of rainfall of up to 80 mm (3.1 in) in some places which were impacted by Hato and Pakhar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mawar1_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mawar1-94">[93]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Guchol_(Kiko)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Guchol_.28Kiko.29">Tropical Storm Guchol (Kiko)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Guchol (Kiko)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg"><img alt="Guchol 2017-09-06 0305Z.jpg" data-file-height="6689" data-file-width="4913" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg/150px-Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg/225px-Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg/300px-Guchol_2017-09-06_0305Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guchol_2017_track.png"><img alt="Guchol 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Guchol_2017_track.png/150px-Guchol_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Guchol_2017_track.png/225px-Guchol_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Guchol_2017_track.png/300px-Guchol_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 3 – September 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 3, the JMA started to track a tropical depression that had developed to the east of <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. During the next day, the PAGASA initiated advisories and gave the local name <i>Kiko</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> while the JTWC followed suit by giving it the designation <i>19W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> However, due to increased wind shear along with an exposed circulation, the JTWC issued its final advisory on 03:00 UTC September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Several hours later, deep convection was depicted and despite moderate to high shear, the JTWC re-initiated advisories,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> while the JMA had upgraded the system to a tropical storm, naming it as <i>Guchol</i> early on the next day. On 21:00 UTC of that day, the JTWC stopped issuing warnings on the system after convection significantly weakened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">JMA later followed suit early in the next day by declaring it a remnant low as it neared <a href="/wiki/Putian" title="Putian">Putian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strait_of_Taiwan" title="Strait of Taiwan">Strait of Taiwan</a>. The remnant low would then make landfall over <a href="/wiki/Pingtan_County" title="Pingtan County">Pingtan County</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> in China late in the following day before it transitioned into an extratropical storm near <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a> as it merged with the cold front on September 8.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Typhoon_Talim_(Lannie)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Talim_.28Lannie.29">Typhoon Talim (Lannie)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Typhoon Talim (Lannie)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg"><img alt="Talim 2017-09-14 0215Z.jpg" data-file-height="7320" data-file-width="5490" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg/150px-Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg/225px-Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg/300px-Talim_2017-09-14_0215Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talim_2017_track.png"><img alt="Talim 2017 track.png" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="2700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Talim_2017_track.png/150px-Talim_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Talim_2017_track.png/225px-Talim_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Talim_2017_track.png/300px-Talim_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 7 – September 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>175 km/h (110 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  935 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical depression formed east of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> on September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> By the next day, the JTWC began issuing advisories on Tropical Depression 20W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> On September 9, 20W organized into a tropical storm, with the JMA naming the system as <i>Talim</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> With gradual intensification, the JMA upgraded Talim to a severe tropical storm. Talim further strengthened to a typhoon on September 11 where it simultaneously entered the PAR, with PAGASA naming it as <i>Lannie</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> The JTWC, however, delayed their upgrade until September 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Due to an ill-defined eye, Talim maintained its intensity until its eye became much clearer as rapid deepening ensued, as Talim became a Category 4 on September 14, and reached its peak intensity with 1-minute sustained winds of 220 km/h (140 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> Talim began to curve eastward as it rapidly weakened to a tropical storm thereafter, making landfall in <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> on September 17, with a path of heavy rainfall up to the region east of Tokyo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of September 18, the death toll from Talim stands at two while 38 are injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talim1_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Talim1-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Typhoon_Doksuri_(Maring)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Doksuri_.28Maring.29">Typhoon Doksuri (Maring)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Typhoon Doksuri (Maring)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg"><img alt="Doksuri 2017-09-14 0548Z.jpg" data-file-height="5872" data-file-width="4536" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg/150px-Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg/225px-Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg/300px-Doksuri_2017-09-14_0548Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Doksuri_2017_track.png"><img alt="Doksuri 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Doksuri_2017_track.png/150px-Doksuri_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Doksuri_2017_track.png/225px-Doksuri_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Doksuri_2017_track.png/300px-Doksuri_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 10 – September 16</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  955 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Doksuri_(2017)" title="Typhoon Doksuri (2017)">Typhoon Doksuri (2017)</a></div>
<p>As of September 19, the NDRRMC confirmed a total of 8 dead due to landslides and flooding while total damages were up to Ph₱267 million (US$5.23 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doksuri1_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doksuri1-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 15, Typhoon Doksuri made landfall in Quảng Bình Province, Vietnam as a Category 3 typhoon. Doksuri killed 15 people so far in Vietnam while estimated damages were about ₫16.36 trillion (US$720 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doksuri2_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doksuri2-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doksuri3_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doksuri3-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doksuri5_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doksuri5-115">[114]</a></sup> Despite making landfall in Indochina, Doksuri affected Hainan and total economic losses were estimated to be CNY 59 million(USD 8.96 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doksuri4_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doksuri4-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Tropical_Depression_22W_(Nando)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_22W_.28Nando.29">Tropical Depression 22W (Nando)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 22W (Nando)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg"><img alt="Nando 2017-09-25 0335Z.jpg" data-file-height="8017" data-file-width="5793" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg/150px-Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg/225px-Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg/300px-Nando_2017-09-25_0335Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nando_2017_track.png"><img alt="Nando 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nando_2017_track.png/150px-Nando_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nando_2017_track.png/225px-Nando_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nando_2017_track.png/300px-Nando_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 23 – September 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>55 km/h (35 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical depression formed to the west of Luzon on September 23, and was named "Nando" by PAGASA. The tropical depression quickly moved west-northwest and made landfall in Quảng Ninh, Vietnam, on September 25, before dissipating later on the same day.</p>
<p>The China Observatory issued a "yellow" alert over in the eastern and southern regions due to rainstorms. Some areas have warned a possible precipitation of about 140 mm (5.5 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> Typhoon Signal No. 1 was raised over in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> during September 24, with expected gusts of up to 70 km/h (42 mph) including rough swells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> A voltage dip also occurred which caused 17 people to be trapped over in lifts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> As the depression approached <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> on September 25, the Vietnam National Center for Hydro-Meteorological Forecasting of Vietnam forecast rainfall of about 150 mm (5.9 in) over in <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> and surrounding provinces, with up to 3 m (9.8 ft) of rough waves over in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ha_Long_bay" title="Ha Long bay">Ha Long bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_systems">Other systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 19, a tropical depression formed close to the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and dissipated over the <a href="/wiki/Sibuyan_Sea" title="Sibuyan Sea">Sibuyan Sea</a> two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Early on June 29, the JMA initiated advisories on a newly formed tropical depression located about 138 km (86 mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> The system re-curved and started moving in a northeastward direction until it dissipated to the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> on July 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Early on July 4, the JMA indicated that a tropical depression had formed about 505 km (314 mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Okinotorishima" title="Okinotorishima">Okinotorishima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> During the next day, the JTWC issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> (TCFA) on the system, although it was canceled several hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> After moving northward, the depression rapidly weakened as it was absorbed by a <a href="/wiki/Stationary_front" title="Stationary front">stationary front</a> on July 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early on July 13, the JMA reported that a non-tropical low had transitioned into a tropical depression about 72 km (45 mi) north-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> The depression moved in a generally northeasterly direction until weakening to a low-pressure area by 06:00 UTC on July 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> A tropical depression formed about 691 km (429 mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> late on July 25, though the JTWC indicated it as a subtropical system with estimated recorded winds of 65 km/h (40 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> After several days, the system had already transitioned into an extratropical cyclone on July 29, without becoming a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> Early on August 25 the JMA started to track a tropical depression over in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> although it was last monitored during the next day when it got absorbed by the outflow of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Pakhar (2017)">Tropical Storm Pakhar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> On August 28, the JMA started to issue advisories on a tropical depression that had developed about 1,217 km (756 mi) east-northeast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuguegarao_City" title="Tuguegarao City">Tuguegarao City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> The JMA predicted that the system would become a tropical storm within the next 24 hours, although because the system did not develop further, the JMA issued their final advisory on 03:00 UTC of August 29 when the system had weakened into a low-pressure area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> The remnants of the system helped with formation of Tropical Storm Mawar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a></div>
<p>Within the Northwest Pacific Ocean, both the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) and PAGASA assign names to tropical cyclones that develop in the Western Pacific, which can result in a tropical cyclone having two names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-138">[137]</a></sup> The Japan Meteorological Agency's RSMC Tokyo — Typhoon Center assigns international names to tropical cyclones on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>'s Typhoon Committee, should they be judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h (40 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-TC-139">[138]</a></sup> PAGASA assigns names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility located between 135°E–115°E and between 5°N–25°N even if the cyclone has had an international name assigned to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-138">[137]</a></sup> The names of significant tropical cyclones are retired, by both <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Philippine typhoon names">PAGASA</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names_(JMA)" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names (JMA)">Typhoon Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-TC-139">[138]</a></sup> Should the list of names for the Philippine region be exhausted then names will be taken from an auxiliary list of which the first ten are published each season. Unused names are marked in <span style="color:#666666">gray</span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_names">International names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: International names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names">List of retired Pacific typhoon names</a></div>
<p>A tropical cyclone is named when it is judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h (40 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> The JMA selected the names from a list of 140 names, that had been developed by the 14 members nations and territories of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names#Background" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names">ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Retired_typhoons_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_typhoons-141">[140]</a></sup> Retired names, if any, will be announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">WMO</a> in 2018; though replacement names will be announced in 2019. The next 28 names on the naming list are listed here along with their international numeric designation, if they are used. During the season the name Hato was used for the first time, after it replaced the name Washi, which was retired after the <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2011 Pacific typhoon season">2011 season</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Philippine typhoon names">List of retired Philippine typhoon names</a></div>
<p>This season, PAGASA will use its own naming scheme for cyclones, that will either develop within or move into their self-defined area of responsibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGASA_Names_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAGASA_Names-142">[141]</a></sup> The names were taken from a list of names, that was last used during <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013</a> and are scheduled to be used again during 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGASA_Names_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-PAGASA_Names-142">[141]</a></sup> All of the names are the same except for Lannie, Salome and Yasmin, which replaced the names <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Utor" title="Typhoon Utor">Labuyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nari_(2013)" title="Typhoon Nari (2013)">Santi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Typhoon Haiyan">Yolanda</a> after they were retired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGASA_Names_142-2"><a href="#cite_note-PAGASA_Names-142">[141]</a></sup> The name Lannie was used for the first time this year.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This table summarizes all the systems that developed within or moved into the northern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, to the west of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> during 2017. The tables also provide an overview of a systems intensity, duration, land areas affected and any deaths or damages associated with the system.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm's intensity of over 33 knots (38 mph, 61 km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2017_Pacific_typhoon_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2017 Pacific typhoon season/ACE calcs">Talk:2017 Pacific typhoon season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-SouthChina-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SouthChina_143-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">South China includes the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Indochina-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Indochina_146-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Indochina is an area in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> which includes <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
